home.</em></font><br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<font color="#052a57"><em>We Americans have a strong belief in democracy.</em></font><br>&nbsp;&nbsp;<font color="#b904af"><b>2.</b></font> used for including yourself and the person you are speaking to in what you are saying or writing<br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<font color="#052a57"><em>Where shall we meet?</em></font><br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<font color="#052a57"><em>Come on, we both need a drink.</em></font><br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<font color="#052a57"><em>In this chapter we shall discuss some aspects of company law.</em></font><br>&nbsp;&nbsp;<font color="#b904af"><b>3.</b></font> used for referring to people in general<br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<font color="#052a57"><em>We live in a competitive world.</em></font><br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<font color="#052a57"><em>How do we learn our mother tongue?</em></font><br>&nbsp;&nbsp;<font color="#b904af"><b>4.</b></font> <font color="#af7f7f">spoken</font> sometimes used instead of ‘you’, especially when a doctor or nurse is speaking to someone who is ill or when a teacher is speaking to children<br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<font color="#052a57"><em>How are we feeling this morning, Mrs Shaw?</em></font><br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<font color="#052a57"><em>Now, do we all have notebooks and pencils?</em></font><br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<font <b><font>his</font></b> <font color="#ff5400">strong</font> <font color="#ff5400">UK</font>  <font color="#21887d">[hɪz]</font> <font color="#ff5400">US</font>  <font color="#ff5400">weak</font> <font <b>he</b> , which can be used in the following ways:<br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;as a possessive determiner (followed by a noun): <font color="#052a57"><em>He gave me his address.</em></font><br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;as a possessive pronoun (without a following noun): <font color="#052a57"><em>My computer didn’t cost as much as his.</em></font> As a possessive pronoun <b>his</b> can refer to a singular or plural noun, and it can be the subject, object, or complement of a verb or the object of a preposition: <font color="#052a57"><em>My car is a Ford, but his is a Fiat.</em></font> <font color="#019444">♦</font> <font color="#052a57"><em>I deal with my problems and he deals with his.</em></font><br>&nbsp;&nbsp;<font color="#b904af"><b>1.</b></font> used for showing that something belongs to or is connected with a man, boy, or male animal that has already been mentioned<br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<font accident.</em></font><br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<font color="#052a57"><em>The house isn’t his: it’s mine.</em></font><br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<font color="#052a57"><em>I saw her parents at the wedding, but I didn’t see his.</em></font><br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<font color="#052a57"><em>The climber fell 1,500 feet to his death.</em></font><br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<b>his own</b><font color="#019444">:</font> <font color="#052a57"><em>Soon he had enough money to set up his own business.</em></font><br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<font color="#019444"><font>Thesaurus:</font></font> <a href="entry://possessive pronouns">possessive pronouns</a><sub><font color="#af7f7f">hyponym</font></sub> <br>&nbsp;&nbsp;<font color="#b904af"><b>2.</b></font> <font color="#af7f7f">old-fashioned</font> used in a general way for showing that something belongs to or is connected with any person, whether they are male or female, especially after a subject such as ‘everyone’, ‘someone’, or ‘anyone’<br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<font color="#052a57"><em>Everyone should use his democratic right to vote.</em></font><br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<font color="#052a57"><em>Each child can choose his favourite story.</em></font><br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<font color="#019444"><font>Thesaurus:</font></font> <a href="entry://possessive pronouns">possessive pronouns</a><sub><font something belongs to or is connected with God<br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<font color="#019444"><font>Thesaurus:</font></font> <a href="entry://names and titles of important christian that
<b><font>that</font></b> <font color="#ff5400">UK</font>  <font color="#21887d">[ðæt]</font> <font color="#ff5400">US</font>  <font color="#6020ae">adverb, conjunction, determiner, pronoun</font> <font color="#ff5400">★★★</font><br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<font color="#019444"><i><font>Summary</font></i></font><br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; <b>That</b> can be used in the following ways:<br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;as a determiner (followed by a noun): <font color="#052a57"><em>Give me that hammer.</em></font><br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;as a demonstrative pronoun (without a following noun): <font color="#052a57"><em>Who gave you that?</em></font><br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;as a conjunction (connecting two clauses): <font color="#052a57"><em>I didn’t know that she was married.</em></font><br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;as a relative pronoun (forming the subject, object, or complement of a relative clause): <font color="#052a57"><em>It’s a song that my mother taught me.</em></font><br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;as an adverb (before an adjective or adverb): <font color="#052a57"><em>Three years? I can’t wait that long.</em></font><br>&nbsp;&nbsp;<font color="#b904af"><b>1.</b></font> <font color="#af7f7f">[</font><font color="#af7f7f"><i>plural</i></font> <font color="#019444">those</font> <font color="#ff5400">UK</font>  <font color="#21887d">[ðəʊz]</font> <font color="#ff5400">US</font>  <font color="#21887d">[ðoʊz]</font><font color="#af7f7f">]</font> <b><font color="#019444">the one that is known about</font></b><br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<font color="#b904af"><b>1a.</b></font> used when you are referring to someone or something that has already been mentioned<br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<font color="#052a57"><em>I know there’s a problem, but I haven’t got time to worry about that now.</em></font><br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<font color="#052a57"><em>No, I’m not in love with Ken. Where did you get that idea?</em></font><br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<font color="#052a57"><em>It was a secret – that’s why they never talked about it.</em></font><br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<font color="#052a57"><em>Why don’t you ask Carmen? That’s who I’d choose.</em></font><br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<font color="#b904af"><b>1b.</b></font> <font color="#af7f7f">spoken</font> used for referring to someone or something that the person you are speaking to already knows about<br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<font color="#052a57"><em>The engine’s started making that noise again.</em></font><br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<font color="#052a57"><em>Why don’t you invite that nice Mr Clifford?</em></font><br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<font to just now?</em></font><br>&nbsp;&nbsp;<font color="#b904af"><b>2.</b></font> <font color="#af7f7f">[</font><font color="#af7f7f"><i>plural</i></font> <font color="#019444">those</font> <font color="#ff5400">UK</font>  <font color="#21887d">[ðəʊz]</font> <font color="#ff5400">US</font>  <font color="#21887d">[ðoʊz]</font><font color="#af7f7f">]</font> <b><font color="#019444">the one that you are looking at</font></b> <font color="#af7f7f">spoken</font><br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<font color="#b904af"><b>2a.</b></font> used for referring to someone or something that is not very near to you but that you can see or point at<br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<font color="#052a57"><em>That’s Jerry’s car, over there.</em></font><br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<font It suits you.</em></font><br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<font color="#052a57"><em>What’s that you’re holding?</em></font><br>&nbsp;&nbsp;<font color="#b904af"><b>3.</b></font> <font color="#af7f7f">[</font><font color="#af7f7f"><i>plural</i></font> <font color="#019444">those</font> <font color="#ff5400">UK</font>  <font color="#21887d">[ðəʊz]</font> <font color="#ff5400">US</font>  <font color="#21887d">[ðoʊz]</font><font color="#af7f7f">]</font> <b><font color="#019444">a past time or event</font></b><br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<font color="#b904af"><b>3a.</b></font> used for referring to a period, event, or experience in the past<br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<font color="#052a57"><em>There were no telephones in those days.</em></font><br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<font color="#052a57"><em>Remember that time we all went to the lake?</em></font><br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<font color="#052a57"><em>He once played for England, but that was a long time ago.</em></font><br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<font color="#b904af"><b>3b.</b></font> used for referring to something that has just happened<br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<font color="#052a57"><em>That was fun. We must do it again some time.</em></font><br>&nbsp;&nbsp;<font color="#b904af"><b>4.</b></font> <font color="#af7f7f">[</font><font color="#af7f7f"><i>plural</i></font> <font color="#019444">those</font> <font color="#ff5400">UK</font> <font color="#21887d">[ðəʊz]</font> <font color="#ff5400">US</font> <font color="#21887d">[ðoʊz]</font><font color="#af7f7f">]</font> <b><font color="#019444">a specific one</font></b> used when you are saying which person or thing you are referring to<br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<font color="#052a57"><em>All the details were in that letter I sent you last week.</em></font><br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<font color="#052a57"><em>Those who could not walk were left to die by the roadside.</em></font><br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<b>that of</b><font color="#019444">:</font> <font color="#052a57"><em>The voice was that of an elderly woman.</em></font><br>&nbsp;&nbsp;<font color="#b904af"><b>5.</b></font> <b><font color="#019444">the person you are talking to</font></b> <font color="#ff5400">British</font> <font color="#af7f7f">spoken</font> used for asking who someone is when you are telephoning them<br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<font color="#052a57"><em>Hello, is that Robert Hoffman? by
<b><font>by</font></b> <font color="#ff5400">UK</font>  <font color="#21887d">[baɪ]</font> <font color="#ff5400">US</font>  <font color="#6020ae">adverb, preposition</font> <font <b><font color="#b904af">▪ <font>I.</font></font> <font>she</font></b> <sup>1</sup> <font color="#ff5400">strong</font> <font color="#ff5400">UK</font>  <font color="#21887d">[ʃiː]</font> <font color="#ff5400">US</font>  <font color="#21887d">[ʃi]</font> <font color="#ff5400">weak</font> <font color="#ff5400">UK</font>  <font color="#21887d">[ʃɪ]</font> <font color="#ff5400">US</font>  <font color="#6020ae">pronoun</font> <font color="#ff5400">★★★</font><br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<font color="#019444"><i><font>Summary</font></i></font><br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; <b>She</b> is used as the subject of a verb. Some people prefer to use <b>she</b> after the verb ‘to be’ but this sounds very formal and old-fashioned: <font color="#052a57"><em>Was it she who spoke to the press?</em></font> In American English, however, ‘This is she’ is the usual way that a woman replies on the telephone when someone asks to speak to her: <font color="#052a57"><em>‘May I speak with Mrs Elpin?’ ‘This is she.’</em></font><br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<font color="#b904af"><b>1.</b></font> used for referring to a woman, girl, or female animal, when they have already been mentioned or when it is obvious which one you are referring to<br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<font color="#052a57"><em>I was with Lisa when she bought her wedding dress.</em></font><br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<font color="#052a57"><em>Our cat’s been bad-tempered since she had kittens.</em></font><br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<font color="#019444"><font>Thesaurus:</font></font> <a href="entry://personal pronouns">personal pronouns</a><sub><font color="#af7f7f">hyponym</font></sub> <br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<font color="#b904af"><b>2.</b></font> <font color="#af7f7f">mainly literary</font> used for referring to a nation, a ship, or a car, when it has already been mentioned or when it is obvious which one you are referring to<br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<font color="#052a57"><em>There were over two thousand people aboard the</em></font><br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<font color="#052a57"><em>Titanic</em></font><br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<font color="#052a57"><em>when she left England.</em></font><br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<font color="#052a57"><em>She’ll do a hundred and twenty miles an hour easily.</em></font><br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<font color="#019444"><font>Thesaurus:</font></font> <a href="entry://personal pronouns">personal pronouns</a><sub><font color="#af7f7f">hyponym</font></sub> <br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<font color="#019444"><font>See also:</font></font> <a href="entry://them">them</a><br><b><font color="#b904af">▪ <font>II.</font></font> she</b> <sup>2</sup> <font color="#ff5400">UK</font>  <font color="#21887d">[ʃiː]</font> <font color="#ff5400">US</font>  <font color="#21887d">[ʃi]</font> <font color="#6020ae">noun</font> <font color="#a64728">[singular]</font> <font color="#af7f7f">spoken</font><br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;a female animal<br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<font color="#052a57"><em>I couldn’t tell if the tortoise was a he or a she.</em></font><br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<font color="#019444"><font>Thesaurus:</font></font> <a href="entry://female animals">female animals</a><sub><font or
<b><font>or</font></b> <font color="#ff5400">UK</font>  <font color="#21887d">[ɔː(r)]</font> <font color="#ff5400">US</font>  <font color="#21887d">[ɔr]</font> <font color="#6020ae">conjunction</font> <font color="#ff5400">★★★</font><br>&nbsp;&nbsp;<font color="#b904af"><b>1.</b></font> <b><font color="#019444">used for showing possibilities or choices</font></b> used for connecting possibilities or choices. In a list, ‘or’ is usually used only before the last possibility or choice<br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<font color="#052a57"><em>Which colour do you want – red, green, yellow, or blue?</em></font><br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<font color="#052a57"><em>He’s probably at lunch or in a meeting.</em></font><br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<b>either... or</b><font color="#019444">:</font> <font color="#052a57"><em>‘When will you get the results?’ ‘Either tomorrow or the day after.’</em></font><br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<b>whether... or</b><font color="#019444">:</font> <font color="#052a57"><em>You don’t care whether he lives or dies, do you?</em></font><br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<b>or not</b><font color="#019444">:</font> <font color="#052a57"><em>The jury must decide whether the prisoner is guilty or not.</em></font><br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<font color="#019444"><font>Thesaurus:</font></font> <a href="entry://conjunctions">conjunctions</a><sub><font color="#af7f7f">hyponym</font></sub> <br>&nbsp;&nbsp;<font color="#b904af"><b>2.</b></font> <b><font color="#019444">and not</font></b> used for including someone or something else in a negative statement<br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<font color="#052a57"><em>She’s had nothing to eat or drink all day.</em></font><br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<font color="#052a57"><em>I never had any help or advice from my parents.</em></font><br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<font color="#019444"><font>Thesaurus:</font></font> <a href="entry://conjunctions">conjunctions</a><sub><font color="#af7f7f">hyponym</font></sub> <br>&nbsp;&nbsp;<font color="#b904af"><b>3.</b></font> <b><font color="#019444">used when amounts or numbers are not exact</font></b> used between two similar numbers for showing that you do not know what the exact number is<br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<b>one or two/​two or three/​three or four etc</b><font color="#019444">:</font> <font color="#052a57"><em>I can photocopy your notes. It’ll only take a minute or two.</em></font><br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<font color="#052a57"><em>The car has to be serviced every five or six thousand miles.</em></font><br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<font color="#019444"><font>Thesaurus:</font></font> <a href="entry://conjunctions">conjunctions</a><sub><font color="#af7f7f">hyponym</font></sub> <br>&nbsp;&nbsp;<font color="#b904af"><b>4.</b></font> <b><font color="#019444">used in warnings, threats, or advice</font></b> used for saying what will happen if someone does not do something<br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<font color="#052a57"><em>The soldiers told everyone to leave or they would be shot.</em></font><br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<b>or else</b><font color="#019444">:</font> <font color="#052a57"><em>We must deal with the problem now, or else it will be too late.</em></font><br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<font color="#052a57"><em>You’d better do what I say, or else</em></font> <font color="#019444">(=I will do something bad to you)</font> <font color="#052a57"><em>.</em></font><br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<font color="#019444"><font>Thesaurus:</font></font> <a href="entry://conjunctions">conjunctions</a><sub><font color="#af7f7f">hyponym</font></sub> <br>&nbsp;&nbsp;<font color="#b904af"><b>5.</b></font> <b><font color="#019444">used when correcting or explaining</font></b> used for introducing a comment that corrects or adds more information to what you have just said<br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<font color="#052a57"><em>There are six cashpoints, or ATMs, in the main airport terminal.</em></font><br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<b>or rather</b><font color="#019444">:</font> <font color="#052a57"><em>This is a problem for the government, or rather for the Prime Minister, to deal with.</em></font><br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<font color="#019444"><font>Thesaurus:</font></font> <a href="entry://conjunctions">conjunctions</a><sub><font color="#af7f7f">hyponym</font></sub> <br>&nbsp;&nbsp;<font color="#b904af"><b>6.</b></font> <b><font color="#019444">used when giving a reason</font></b> used when you are trying to show that something must be true, by saying that the situation would be different if it was not true<br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<font color="#052a57"><em>He obviously doesn’t have a plan, or he would have said something.</em></font><br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<b>or else</b><font color="#019444">:</font> <font color="#052a57"><em>It must be something serious, or else they wouldn’t as
<b><font>as</font></b> <font color="#ff5400">strong</font> <font color="#ff5400">UK</font>  <font color="#21887d">[æz]</font> <font color="#ff5400">US</font>  <font color="#ff5400">weak</font> <font color="#ff5400">★★★</font><br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<font color="#019444"><i><font>Summary</font></i></font><br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; <b>As</b> can be used in the following ways:<br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;as a conjunction (connecting two clauses): <font color="#052a57"><em>As I was leaving, the phone rang.</em></font> <font color="#019444">♦</font> <font color="#052a57"><em>The results were not as bad as I had expected.</em></font><br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;as a preposition (followed by a noun): <font color="#052a57"><em>He works as a waiter.</em></font><br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;as an adverb (followed by an adjective, an adverb, or a word such as ‘much’ or ‘many’): <font color="#052a57"><em>Nylon is cheaper than leather, and it’s just as strong.</em></font><br>&nbsp;&nbsp;<font color="#b904af"><b>1.</b></font> <b><font color="#019444">used for showing comparison</font></b><br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<font color="#052a57"><em>Simon isn’t as tall as his brother.</em></font><br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<font color="#052a57"><em>I don’t play football as much as I used to.</em></font><br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<font color="#052a57"><em>I can’t run as fast as you.</em></font><br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<b>just as</b><font color="#019444">:</font> <font color="#052a57"><em>We all need regular exercise, but a healthy diet is just as important.</em></font><br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<b>half/​twice/​three times etc as much</b><font color="#019444">:</font> <font color="#052a57"><em>A house in London costs twice as much as a similar house in Liverpool.</em></font><br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<b>the same as</b><font color="#019444">:</font> <font color="#052a57"><em>Barbara’s suggestion was almost exactly the same as mine.</em></font><br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<font color="#b904af"><b>1b.</b></font> used in particular expressions for emphasizing a quality in someone or something<br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<font color="#052a57"><em>Her skin was white as snow.</em></font><br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<font color="#052a57"><em>as tough as old boots</em></font><br>&nbsp;&nbsp;<font color="#b904af"><b>2.</b></font> <b><font color="#019444">used for referring to what is known</font></b> <font color="#af7f7f">spoken</font> used for mentioning that something is already known or has already been talked about<br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<font color="#052a57"><em>As I was saying, we expect next year to be a good year.</em></font><br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<font color="#052a57"><em>As everyone knows, the farming industry is in serious difficulties.</em></font><br>&nbsp;&nbsp;<font color="#b904af"><b>3.</b></font> <b><font color="#019444">in the same way</font></b> used for saying that something happens or is done in the same way<br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<font color="#052a57"><em>I invested the money as you suggested.</em></font><br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<font color="#052a57"><em>Leave everything just as you found it.</em></font><br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<b>as usual</b><font color="#019444">:</font> <font color="#052a57"><em>Judith was late, as usual.</em></font><br>&nbsp;&nbsp;<font color="#b904af"><b>4.</b></font> <b><font color="#019444">having a particular job, use, or appearance</font></b> used for referring to what someone or something does or how they appear<br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<font color="#052a57"><em>As managing director, I am expected to provide effective leadership.</em></font><br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<font color="#052a57"><em>a portrait of the princess as a child</em></font><br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<font color="#052a57"><em>An electric drill can also be used as a screwdriver.</em></font><br>&nbsp;&nbsp;<font way<br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<font color="#052a57"><em>Van Dyck was regarded as the greatest painter of his time.</em></font><br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<font down to dinner, the phone rang.</em></font><br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<b>just as</b><font color="#019444">:</font> <font color="#052a57"><em>We got to the check-in desk just as they were something<br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<font color="#052a57"><em>As it was getting late, we decided to go home.</em></font><br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<font what
<b><font>what</font></b> <font color="#ff5400">UK</font>  <font color="#21887d">[wɒt]</font> <font color="#ff5400">US</font>  <font color="#21887d">[wɑt]</font> <font color="#ff5400">US</font>  <font color="#21887d">[hwɑt]</font> <font color="#6020ae">adverb, determiner, interjection, predeterminer, pronoun</font> <font color="#ff5400">★★★</font><br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<font color="#019444"><i><font>Summary</font></i></font><br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; <b>What</b> can be used in the following ways:<br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;as a question pronoun (introducing a direct or indirect question): <font color="#052a57"><em>What do you want?</em></font> <font color="#019444">♦</font> <font color="#052a57"><em>Tell me what happened.</em></font><br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;as a relative pronoun (starting a relative clause that is subject, object, or complement of another clause): <font color="#052a57"><em>She showed me what she had bought.</em></font><br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;as a determiner (followed by a noun and introducing a question): <font color="#052a57"><em>What subjects are you studying?</em></font> (followed by a noun and introducing a relative clause): <font color="#052a57"><em>I’ll give you what money I have.</em></font><br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;as a predeterminer (before ‘a’, ‘an’, or ‘the’): <font color="#052a57"><em>What a nuisance!</em></font><br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;as an adverb : <font color="#052a57"><em>What does it matter?</em></font><br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;as an interjection : <font color="#052a57"><em>What! You mean I’ve been wasting my time?</em></font><br>&nbsp;&nbsp;<font color="#b904af"><b>1.</b></font> <b><font color="#019444">which thing</font></b><br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<font color="#b904af"><b>1a.</b></font> used for asking which thing, action, or idea something is, or which type of thing, action, or idea something is<br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<font color="#052a57"><em>What’s your name?</em></font><br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<font color="#052a57"><em>What time is it?</em></font><br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<font color="#052a57"><em>What was the weather like?</em></font><br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<font color="#052a57"><em>I asked her what kind of music she liked.</em></font><br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<font color="#052a57"><em>People sometimes ask me what I’m going to do when I retire.</em></font><br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<font color="#052a57"><em>‘I’m worried, Harry.’ ‘What about?’</em></font><br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<font color="#019444"><font>Thesaurus:</font></font> <a href="entry://ways of asking questions and making requests">ways of asking questions and making requests</a><sub><font color="#af7f7f">hyponym</font></sub> <a href="entry://to ask a question or questions">to ask a question or questions</a><sub><font color="#af7f7f">synonym</font></sub> <br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<font color="#b904af"><b>1b.</b></font> used when someone knows or says which thing, action, or idea something is<br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<font color="#052a57"><em>I told him what the problem was.</em></font><br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<font color="#052a57"><em>She wasn’t quite sure what she was going to say.</em></font><br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<font color="#052a57"><em>We suddenly realized what was happening.</em></font><br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<font color="#052a57"><em>I haven’t even thought about what I’m going to wear to the dinner.</em></font><br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<b>what to do/​say/​think etc</b><font color="#019444">:</font> <font color="#052a57"><em>Poor Kevin! He doesn’t know what to do.</em></font><br>&nbsp;&nbsp;<font color="#b904af"><b>2.</b></font> <b><font color="#019444">a particular thing</font></b> used for referring to a particular thing, action, or idea<br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<font color="#052a57"><em>You haven’t given me what I asked for.</em></font><br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<font color="#052a57"><em>What you need is a good long holiday.</em></font><br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<font color="#052a57"><em>What annoys me is the way he boasts about what he’s done.</em></font><br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<font color="#052a57"><em>George always does his best, and that’s what I like about him.</em></font><br>&nbsp;&nbsp;<font color="#b904af"><b>3.</b></font> <b><font color="#019444">all of an amount</font></b> used for referring to the whole amount that remains or is available<br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<font color="#052a57"><em>Tom eagerly finished up what was left of the champagne and chicken pie.</em></font><br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<font color="#052a57"><em>What little free time he had was spent with the family.</em></font><br>&nbsp;&nbsp;<font color="#b904af"><b>4.</b></font> <b><font color="#019444">used for emphasizing a quality</font></b> <font color="#af7f7f">spoken</font> used for introducing a remark in which you emphasize how big, good, bad etc someone or something is<br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<font color="#052a57"><em>What awful weather we’ve been having!</em></font><br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<font color="#052a57"><em>What a nice surprise!</em></font><br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<font color="#052a57"><em>What a nuisance for you, having to make all these changes.</em></font><br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<font color="#019444"><font>Thesaurus:</font></font> <a href="entry://ways of emphasizing what you are their
<b><font>their</font></b> <font color="#ff5400">UK</font>  <font color="#21887d">[ðeə(r)]</font> <font color="#ff5400">US</font>  <font color="#21887d">[ðer]</font> <font color="#6020ae">determiner</font> <font color="#ff5400">★★★</font><br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<font color="#019444"><i><font>Summary</font></i></font><br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; <b>Their</b> is used as a possessive determiner (followed by a noun), being a possessive form of <b>they</b> . <br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<font color="#019444"><i><font><br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Get it right: their </font></i></font>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Don’t confuse <b>their </b> (the possessive form of ‘they’) and <b>there </b> (a pronoun and adverb). These two words sound exactly the same.<br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<font>✗</font><font color="#052a57"><em> In a democracy, people have the power to decide </em></font> <b><font color="#052a57"><em>there</em></font> </b> <font color="#052a57"><em>own future.</em></font><br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<font color="green">✓</font><font color="#052a57"><em> In a democracy, people have the power to decide </em></font> <b><font color="#052a57"><em>their</em></font> </b> <font color="#052a57"><em>own future.</em></font><br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<font>✗</font><font color="#052a57"><em> Most women didn’t work and were dependent on </em></font> <b><font color="#052a57"><em>there</em></font> </b> <font color="#052a57"><em>husbands.</em></font><br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<font color="green">✓</font><font color="#052a57"><em> Most women didn’t work and were dependent on </em></font> <b><font color="#052a57"><em>their</em></font> </b> <font color="#052a57"><em>husbands.</em></font> <br>&nbsp;&nbsp;<font color="#b904af"><b>1.</b></font> belonging to or relating to a particular group of people or things that have already been mentioned or when it is obvious which ones you are referring to<br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<font color="#052a57"><em>Workers are afraid that they will lose their jobs.</em></font><br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<font color="#052a57"><em>She has made a study of chemical fertilizers and their effect on the environment.</em></font><br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<b>of their own</b><font color="#019444">:</font> <font color="#052a57"><em>They have children of their own.</em></font><br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<font color="#019444"><font>Thesaurus:</font></font> <a href="entry://determiners">determiners</a><sub><font color="#af7f7f">hyponym</font></sub> <br>&nbsp;&nbsp;<font color="#b904af"><b>2.</b></font> <font color="#af7f7f">mainly spoken</font> used instead of ‘his or her’, especially when you are referring back to a word such as ‘everyone’, ‘someone’, or ‘anyone’ Many people consider this use incorrect<br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<font color="#052a57"><em>Everyone has their own way of doing things.</em></font><br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<font color="#019444"><font>Thesaurus:</font></font> <a href="entry://determiners">determiners</a><sub><font color="#af7f7f">hyponym</font></sub> <br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<font color="#019444"><font>See also:</font></font> <a href="entry://they">they</a>

can
<b><font color="#b904af">▪ <font>I.</font></font> <font>can</font></b> <sup>1</sup> <font color="#ff5400">strong</font> <font color="#ff5400">UK</font>  <font color="#21887d">[kæn]</font> <font color="#ff5400">US</font>  <font color="#ff5400">weak</font> <font color="#ff5400">UK</font>  <font color="#21887d">[kən]</font> <font color="#ff5400">US</font>  <font color="#6020ae">modal verb</font> <font color="#ff5400">★★★</font><br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<font color="#019444"><i><font>Summary</font></i></font><br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; <b>Can</b> is usually followed by an infinitive without ‘to’: <font color="#052a57"><em>I can speak French.</em></font> Sometimes it is used without a following infinitive: <font color="#052a57"><em>Come and help us, if you can.</em></font><br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; <b>Can</b> does not change its form, so the third person singular form does not end in ‘-s’: <font color="#052a57"><em>She can speak Japanese.</em></font><br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Questions and negatives are formed without ‘do’: <font color="#052a57"><em>Can you swim?</em></font><br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;The negative form of <b>can</b> is <b>cannot</b> : <font color="#052a57"><em>We cannot allow this behaviour to continue.</em></font> <b>Cannot</b> is often shortened in conversation or informal writing to <b>can’t</b> : <font color="#052a57"><em>I can’t find my brown jacket.</em></font><br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; <b>Can</b> is often used in question tags: <font color="#052a57"><em>They can’t hear us, can they?</em></font><br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; <b>Can</b> has no participles and no infinitive form. <b>Be able to</b> is used as the infinitive to show ability or possibility: <font color="#052a57"><em>I want to be able to choose my own career.</em></font><br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; <b>Could</b> is used as the past tense of <b>can</b> when it means that someone had the ability to do something, or that something was possible: <font color="#052a57"><em>New York was a place where anyone could start a business.</em></font> But <b>was/​were able to</b> is used for saying that someone actually succeeded in doing something: <font color="#052a57"><em>By climbing on the table he was able to reach the window.</em></font><br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;There is no future tense of <b>can</b> , but <b>will be able to</b> is used for saying that someone will have the ability to do something or that something will be possible in the future, especially after a long time: <font color="#052a57"><em>She’ll be able to walk soon.</em></font> <font color="#019444">♦</font> <font color="#052a57"><em>A hundred years from now people will be able to visit Mars.</em></font> <b>Can</b> is usually used when planning or deciding about the near future: <font color="#052a57"><em>We can go shopping tomorrow.</em></font><br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;There is no perfect tense of <b>can</b> , so <b>has/​have been able to</b> is used: <font color="#052a57"><em>I haven’t been able to phone my parents yet.</em></font> <br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<font color="#019444"><i><font><br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Get it right: can </font></i></font>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;The negative form of the verb can is <b>cannot </b> . It is written almost always as one word, not as ‘can not’ (two words):<br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<i><b><font color="#052a57"><em>?</em></font> </b> </i> <font guaranteed.</em></font><br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<font color="green">✓</font><font color="#052a57"><em> The quality of the information </em></font> <b><font </i> <font color="#052a57"><em>You</em></font> <b><font color="#052a57"><em>can not</em></font> </b> <font color="#052a57"><em>buy true friends or health.</em></font><br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<font color="green">✓</font><font color="#052a57"><em> You </em></font> <b><font color="#052a57"><em>cannot</em></font> </b> who
<b><font>who</font></b> <font color="#ff5400">UK</font>  <font color="#21887d">[huː]</font> <font color="#ff5400">US</font>  <font color="#21887d">[hu]</font> <font color="#6020ae">pronoun</font> <font color="#ff5400">★★★</font><br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<font color="#019444"><i><font>Summary</font></i></font><br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; <b>Who</b> can be used in the following ways:<br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;as a question pronoun (introducing a direct or indirect question): <font color="#052a57"><em>Who’s going to drive?</em></font> <font color="#019444">♦</font> <font color="#052a57"><em>I wonder who they chose to be captain.</em></font> <font color="#019444">♦</font> <font color="#052a57"><em>Who did you give the money to?</em></font><br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;as a relative pronoun (referring back to a person and starting a relative clause): <font color="#052a57"><em>I want to speak to the person who deals with my account.</em></font> <font color="#019444">♦</font> <font color="#052a57"><em>She was with her husband, who I had already met.</em></font> (starting a relative clause that is the subject, object, or complement of another clause): <font color="#052a57"><em>I don’t know who she is.</em></font><br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Notice that <b>who</b> can be used as the subject or object of a verb or preposition. In formal English <b>whom</b> is sometimes used instead of <b>who</b> as the object of a verb or preposition, but it sounds very formal to say: <font color="#052a57"><em>To whom did you speak?</em></font> It is more normal to put the preposition at the end and say: <font color="#052a57"><em>Who did you speak to?</em></font> <br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<font color="#019444"><i><font><br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Get it right: who </font></i></font>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Don’t confuse <b>who’s </b> (the short form of ‘who is’ or ‘who has’) with <b>whose </b> (the possessive form of ‘who’, meaning ‘of whom’ or ‘of which’):<br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<font>✗</font><font color="#052a57"><em> </em></font> <b><font color="#052a57"><em>Who’s view</em></font> </b> <font color="#052a57"><em>of the facts are we getting through television?</em></font><br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<font color="green">✓</font><font color="#052a57"><em> </em></font> <b><font color="#052a57"><em>Whose view</em></font> </b> <font color="#052a57"><em>of the facts are we getting through television?</em></font><br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<font>✗</font><font color="#052a57"><em> …an international organization </em></font> <b><font color="#052a57"><em>who’s role</em></font> </b> <font color="#052a57"><em>is to keep peace and stability.</em></font><br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<font color="green">✓</font><font color="#052a57"><em> …an international organization </em></font> <b><font color="#052a57"><em>whose role</em></font> </b> <font color="#052a57"><em>is to keep peace and stability.</em></font><br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;The short form <b>who’s </b> (‘who is’ or ‘who has’) is used mainly in spoken English and informal writing:<br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<font color="#052a57"><em>‘</em></font> <b><font color="#052a57"><em>Who’s going</em></font> </b> <font color="#052a57"><em>to do that?’ ‘You, of course.’</em></font><br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<b><font color="#052a57"><em>Who’s been</em></font> </b> <font color="#052a57"><em>using my computer?</em></font> <br>&nbsp;&nbsp;<font color="#b904af"><b>1.</b></font> used for asking which person is involved in something, or what someone’s name is<br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<font color="#052a57"><em>Who does this place belong to?</em></font><br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<font color="#052a57"><em>Who killed John F. Kennedy?</em></font><br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<font color="#052a57"><em>Who was that guy I saw you with last night?</em></font><br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<font color="#052a57"><em>Who did you hire for the sales position?</em></font><br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<font color="#052a57"><em>Do you know who’s been invited to Claire’s dinner party?</em></font><br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<font color="#052a57"><em>‘Who is that?’ ‘It’s Karen – don’t you recognize her?’</em></font><br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<b>who else</b> <font color="#019444">(=which other person)</font><font color="#019444">:</font> <font color="#052a57"><em>Who else did you tell the secret to?</em></font><br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<font color="#019444"><font>Thesaurus:</font></font> <a href="entry://pronouns">pronouns</a><sub><font color="#af7f7f">hyponym</font></sub> <br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<font color="#b904af"><b>1a.</b></font> used when someone knows or says which person is involved in something or what their name is<br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<font color="#052a57"><em>They’ve already offered the job to someone, but I don’t know who.</em></font><br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<font color="#052a57"><em>Curry refused to say who had organized the meeting.</em></font><br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<font color="#052a57"><em>We have to be very careful who we deal with.</em></font><br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<font color="#052a57"><em>Martha won’t say who she voted for.</em></font><br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<font color="#019444"><font>Thesaurus:</font></font> <a href="entry://pronouns">pronouns</a><sub><font color="#af7f7f">hyponym</font></sub> <br>&nbsp;&nbsp;<font color="#b904af"><b>2.</b></font> used for adding information that shows which person or type of person you are talking about It is more usual to use ‘that’ to introduce this type of relative clause<br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<font color="#052a57"><em>We only employ people who already have computer skills.</em></font><br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<font color="#052a57"><em>We got the same answer from everyone who we spoke to.</em></font><br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<font color="#052a57"><em>I think Bramwell was the one who first suggested the idea.</em></font><br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<font color="#019444"><i><font><br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Usage note </font></i></font>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;The relative pronoun <b>who</b> or <b>whom</b> is often left out when it is the object in this type of relative clause: <font color="#052a57"><em>You are free to marry the man (who/​whom) you love.</em></font><br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<font color="#019444"><font>Thesaurus:</font></font> <a href="entry://pronouns">pronouns</a><sub><font color="#af7f7f">hyponym</font></sub> <br>&nbsp;&nbsp;<font color="#b904af"><b>3.</b></font> used for adding more information about a person when it is already clear which person you are talking about<br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<font color="#052a57"><em>I recently talked to Michael Hall, who lectures in music at the university.</em></font><br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<font color="#052a57"><em>I want you to meet my friend Marjorie, who I think I mentioned in my last letter.</em></font><br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<font color="#019444"><font>Thesaurus:</font></font> <a href="entry://pronouns">pronouns</a><sub><font color="#af7f7f">hyponym</font></sub> if
<b><font color="#b904af">▪ <font>I.</font></font> <font>if</font></b> <sup>1</sup> <font color="#ff5400">UK</font>  <font color="#21887d">[ɪf]</font> <font color="#ff5400">US</font>  <font color="#6020ae">conjunction</font> <font color="#ff5400">★★★</font><br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<font color="#b904af"><b>1.</b></font> <b><font color="#019444">in a possible or imagined situation</font></b><br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<font color="#b904af"><b>1a.</b></font> used for introducing a situation that may happen or may be real, especially when talking about its results<br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<font color="#052a57"><em>If we miss the last bus, we’ll have to walk home.</em></font><br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<font color="#052a57"><em>If anyone has found a bunch of keys, would they please leave them on my desk.</em></font><br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<b>if you want/​like</b><font color="#019444">:</font> <font color="#052a57"><em>You can come and stay with us if you want.</em></font><br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<b>if so</b> <font color="#019444">(=if this is true)</font><font color="#019444">:</font> <font color="#052a57"><em>Are you planning to return to work, and if so, who is going to look after the baby?</em></font><br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<b>if not</b> <font color="#019444">(=if this is not true)</font><font color="#019444">:</font> <font color="#052a57"><em>Has anyone dealt with the technical problems? And if not, why not?</em></font><br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<b>if necessary/​if possible</b> <font color="#019444">(=if it is necessary/​possible)</font><font color="#019444">:</font> <font color="#052a57"><em>We are ready to fight for our rights if necessary.</em></font><br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<font color="#052a57"><em>I should like to be back here by 10.30 if possible.</em></font><br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<font color="#019444"><font>Thesaurus:</font></font> <a href="entry://conjunctions">conjunctions</a><sub><font color="#af7f7f">hyponym</font></sub> <br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<font color="#b904af"><b>1b.</b></font> used for introducing a situation or condition that must exist before something else happens<br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<font color="#052a57"><em>Okay I’ll come with you if you’ll promise not to go too fast.</em></font><br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<b>only if</b><font color="#019444">:</font> <font color="#052a57"><em>The rebels say they are ready to stop fighting, but only if the prisoners are released.</em></font><br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<font color="#019444"><font>Thesaurus:</font></font> <a href="entry://conjunctions">conjunctions</a><sub><font color="#af7f7f">hyponym</font></sub> <br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<font color="#b904af"><b>1c.</b></font> used for introducing a situation that does not exist now and is unlikely or impossible, especially when talking about its imaginary results<br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<font color="#052a57"><em>If Luke paid more attention in class, he would achieve better results.</em></font><br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<font color="#052a57"><em>If Freud were alive today, he would approve of our methods.</em></font><br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<font color="#052a57"><em>If you should happen to meet Diane, would you give her a message.</em></font><br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<font color="#052a57"><em>If anyone were to complain, I should merely tell them to write to the manager.</em></font><br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<b>even if</b><font color="#019444">:</font> <font color="#052a57"><em>I’d never sell this painting, even if they offered me a million dollars.</em></font><br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<font color="#019444"><font>Thesaurus:</font></font> <a href="entry://conjunctions">conjunctions</a><sub><font color="#af7f7f">hyponym</font></sub> <br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<font color="#b904af"><b>1d.</b></font> used for introducing a situation that might have existed in the past but did not exist, especially when talking about what its results might have been<br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<font color="#052a57"><em>If I’d known you were coming, I would have had a meal ready for you.</em></font><br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<font color="#052a57"><em>If the new safety system had been in use, the accident would never have happened.</em></font><br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<font color="#019444"><font>Thesaurus:</font></font> <a href="entry://conjunctions">conjunctions</a><sub><font color="#af7f7f">hyponym</font></sub> <br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<font color="#b904af"><b>2.</b></font> <b><font color="#019444">used when something is always true</font></b> used for introducing a situation that always has the same result, meaning, or effect<br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<font color="#052a57"><em>I always get a headache if I watch too much television.</em></font><br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<font color="#052a57"><em>If you drive without insurance, you’re breaking the law.</em></font><br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<font color="#019444"><font>Thesaurus:</font></font> <a href="entry://conjunctions">conjunctions</a><sub><font color="#af7f7f">hyponym</font></sub> <br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<font color="#b904af"><b>3.</b></font> <b><font color="#019444">whether</font></b><br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<font color="#b904af"><b>3a.</b></font> used in indirect questions that ask whether something is true<br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<font color="#052a57"><em>She asked me if I was fond of music.</em></font><br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<font color="#052a57"><em>Can you tell me if they’re planning to come?</em></font><br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<font color="#019444"><font>Thesaurus:</font></font> <a href="entry://conjunctions">conjunctions</a><sub><font certain<br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<font color="#052a57"><em>I doubt if anyone will be interested in the programme.</em></font><br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<font color="#052a57"><em>Palmer still hasn’t decided if he’s going to play in Saturday’s match.</em></font><br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<font color="#019444"><font>Thesaurus:</font></font> <a href="entry://conjunctions">conjunctions</a><sub><font introducing the reason that you think someone may want to know something<br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<font color="#052a57"><em>There are plenty of taxis if you’re in a hurry.</em></font><br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<font color="#052a57"><em>If you really want to know, I’m fed up with this stupid job.</em></font><br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<font color="#052a57"><em>If anyone asks you where I am, I’ll be in the library.</em></font><br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<font color="#019444"><font>Thesaurus:</font></font> <a href="entry://conjunctions">conjunctions</a><sub><font color="#af7f7f">hyponym</font></sub> <br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<font color="#b904af"><b>5.</b></font> <b><font color="#019444">used for saying how you feel about a possibility</font></b><br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<font color="#b904af"><b>5a.</b></font> used for saying how you feel about the possibility that something may happen or be true<br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<font color="#052a57"><em>I’m sorry if I’ve said anything that has caused offence.</em></font><br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<font color="#052a57"><em>I don’t care if I never see her again.</em></font><br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<font color="#019444"><font>Thesaurus:</font></font> <a href="entry://conjunctions">conjunctions</a><sub><font color="#af7f7f">hyponym</font></sub> <br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<font color="#b904af"><b>5b.</b></font> used when expressing an opinion about an imagined situation<br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<font color="#052a57"><em>It would be a pity if they had to cancel the show.</em></font><br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<font color="#052a57"><em>Wouldn’t it be nice if we could spend more time with the children?</em></font><br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<font color="#019444"><font>Thesaurus:</font></font> <a href="entry://conjunctions">conjunctions</a><sub><font color="#af7f7f">hyponym</font></sub> <br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<font color="#b904af"><b>6.</b></font> <b><font color="#019444">used in requests</font></b> <font color="#af7f7f">spoken</font><br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<font color="#b904af"><b>6a.</b></font> used when politely asking someone to do something or when asking for permission to do something<br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<font color="#052a57"><em>I would be grateful if you would send me further details of the programme.</em></font><br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<b>if you don’t mind/​if it’s all right with you</b><font color="#019444">:</font> <font color="#052a57"><em>If you don’t mind, I’d like to sit at the back.</em></font><br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<font color="#019444"><font>Thesaurus:</font></font> <a href="entry://conjunctions">conjunctions</a><sub><font color="#af7f7f">hyponym</font></sub> <br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<font color="#b904af"><b>6b.</b></font> used when politely trying to add something to a conversation or discussion<br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<font color="#052a57"><em>If I could just make a suggestion – why don’t we invite Andrew to our next color="#af7f7f">hyponym</font></sub> <br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<font color="#b904af"><b>7.</b></font> <b><font color="#019444">although perhaps</font></b> used for introducing a remark that makes your description seem slightly less positive or certain<br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<font color="#052a57"><em>The stories are basically true, if a little something that someone may have noticed, before explaining the reason for it<br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<font color="#052a57"><em>If I seem angry sometimes, it’s usually because I’m very tired.</em></font><br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<font color="#019444"><font>Thesaurus:</font></font> <a href="entry://conjunctions">conjunctions</a><sub><font color="#af7f7f">hyponym</font></sub> <br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<font color="#b904af"><b>9.</b></font> <b><font color="#019444">possibly more, or possibly less</font></b> used for suggesting that something may possibly be more or less, better or worse etc than you have stated<br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<font color="#052a57"><em>Fodor’s predictions have seldom if ever been proved wrong.</em></font><br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<b>if not</b><font color="#019444">:</font> <font color="#052a57"><em>The changes will affect thousands, if not showing surprise</font></b> <font color="#af7f7f">spoken</font> used for introducing a negative expression to emphasize that you think something is very surprising or would
<b><font>would</font></b> <font color="#ff5400">UK</font>  <font color="#21887d">[wʊd]</font> <font color="#ff5400">US</font>  <font color="#6020ae">modal verb</font> <font color="#ff5400">★★★</font><br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<font color="#019444"><i><font>Summary</font></i></font><br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; <b>Would</b> is usually followed by an infinitive without ‘to’: <font color="#052a57"><em>A picnic would be nice.</em></font> Sometimes it is used without a following infinitive: <font color="#052a57"><em>They didn’t do as much as they said they would.</em></font><br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;In conversation and informal writing, <b>would</b> is often shortened to <b>’d</b> : <font color="#052a57"><em>I thought you’d like a drink before dinner.</em></font><br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; <b>Would</b> does not change its form, so the third person singular form does not end in ‘-s’: <font color="#052a57"><em>As a child, she would often run away from home.</em></font><br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Questions and negatives are formed without ‘do’: <font color="#052a57"><em>Would you like a cup of coffee?</em></font> <font color="#019444">♦</font> <font color="#052a57"><em>He would not tell us his secret.</em></font><br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;The negative form <b>would not</b> is often shortened in conversation or informal writing to <b>wouldn’t</b> : <font color="#052a57"><em>I wouldn’t want to have your job.</em></font><br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; <b>Would</b> is often used in question tags: <font color="#052a57"><em>You wouldn’t lie to me, would you?</em></font><br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; <b>Would</b> has no tenses, no participles, and no infinitive form.<br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;There is no past tense, but <b>would have</b> followed by a past participle can be used for talking about actions that did not happen: <font color="#052a57"><em>She would have bought the house if she had been able to afford it</em></font> (=she did not buy it).<br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;In some cases <b>would</b> can be used as the past tense of <b>will</b> , for example in indirect speech introduced by a verb in the past tense: <font color="#052a57"><em>I promised that I would visit her the next day.</em></font> <br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<font color="#019444"><i><font><br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Learner Errors </font></i></font>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;In requests and offers <a href="entry://would">would</a> can be used with the same meaning as <a href="entry://will">will</a> but in a more polite or less definite way: <font color="#052a57"><em>Would/​Will you please help me?</em></font> <font color="#019444">♦</font> <font color="#052a57"><em>I would/​will be glad to answer any questions.</em></font><br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Should is sometimes used instead of <a href="entry://would">would</a> when the subject is ‘I’ or ‘we’: <font color="#052a57"><em>We would/​should be grateful if you would send us more information.</em></font> <font color="#019444">♦</font> <font color="#052a57"><em>I would/​should think you are tired after your long journey.</em></font> <br>&nbsp;&nbsp;<font color="#b904af"><b>1.</b></font> <b><font color="#019444">used for talking about what was going to happen in the past</font></b><br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<font color="#b904af"><b>1a.</b></font> used for showing what someone expected, intended, promised etc when they were thinking or talking about the future<br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<font color="#052a57"><em>James said he would never forgive her.</em></font><br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<font color="#052a57"><em>Most analysts expected that there would be a change in policy.</em></font><br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<font color="#052a57"><em>‘Our plan isn’t going to work.’ ‘I never thought it would.’</em></font><br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<font color="#019444"><font>Thesaurus:</font></font> <a href="entry://modal verbs">modal verbs</a><sub><font color="#af7f7f">hyponym</font></sub> <br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<font color="#b904af"><b>1b.</b></font> used for talking about something that was going to happen after a particular point in the past<br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<font color="#052a57"><em>Here she met the man who would one day become her husband.</em></font><br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<font color="#019444"><font>Thesaurus:</font></font> <a href="entry://modal verbs">modal verbs</a><sub><font color="#af7f7f">hyponym</font></sub> <br>&nbsp;&nbsp;<font color="#b904af"><b>2.</b></font> <b><font color="#019444">used for talking about results of an unlikely situation</font></b> used for talking about the possible results of a situation that is unlikely to happen or that did not happen<br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<font color="#052a57"><em>I’d travel first class if I could afford it.</em></font><br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<font color="#052a57"><em>What would happen if there was an earthquake?</em></font><br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<b>would have done something</b><font color="#019444">:</font> <font color="#052a57"><em>If I’d known you were coming, I’d have got your room ready.</em></font><br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<font color="#019444"><font>Thesaurus:</font></font> <a href="entry://modal verbs">modal verbs</a><sub><font color="#af7f7f">hyponym</font></sub> <br>&nbsp;&nbsp;<font color="#b904af"><b>3.</b></font> <b><font color="#019444">used for asking or giving opinions</font></b> used for saying or asking what someone thinks about a possible situation<br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<font color="#052a57"><em>You wouldn’t recognize the place now – it’s changed so much.</em></font><br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<font color="#052a57"><em>It would be fun to have a beach party.</em></font><br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<font color="#052a57"><em>It’s no use talking to Henry – he wouldn’t understand.</em></font><br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<font color="#052a57"><em>Why would anyone want to kill Jerry?</em></font><br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<font color="#052a57"><em>Where would he have hidden the keys?</em></font><br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<font color="#052a57"><em>I could lend you some – would fifty pounds be enough?</em></font><br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<font color="#019444"><font>Thesaurus:</font></font> <a href="entry://modal verbs">modal verbs</a><sub><font color="#af7f7f">hyponym</font></sub> <br>&nbsp;&nbsp;<font color="#b904af"><b>4.</b></font> <b><font color="#019444">used for talking about past habits</font></b> used for saying what someone used to do in the past<br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<font color="#052a57"><em>The Campbells would sometimes invite us over for the weekend.</em></font><br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<font color="#052a57"><em>On winter evenings we’d all sit around the fire.</em></font><br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<font color="#019444"><font>Thesaurus:</font></font> <a href="entry://modal verbs">modal verbs</a><sub><font color="#af7f7f">hyponym</font></sub> <br>&nbsp;&nbsp;<font color="#b904af"><b>5.</b></font> <b><font color="#019444">used for criticizing someone’s behaviour</font></b> <font color="#af7f7f">spoken</font> used when criticizing someone by saying that a particular action is typical of someone<br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<font color="#052a57"><em>‘Sylvia said it was your fault.’ ‘Well, Sylvia would say that, wouldn’t she?’</em></font><br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<font color="#019444"><font>Thesaurus:</font></font> <a href="entry://ways of making or receiving criticism or blame">ways of making or receiving criticism or blame</a><sub><font color="#af7f7f">hyponym</font></sub> <a href="entry://to criticize, accuse or blame">to criticize, accuse or blame</a><sub><font color="#af7f7f">synonym</font></sub> <br>&nbsp;&nbsp;<font color="#b904af"><b>6.</b></font> <b><font color="#019444">used in requests</font></b> used for politely asking someone to do something or to let you do something<br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<font color="#052a57"><em>Would someone please help me move the piano?</em></font><br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<b>would you mind doing something</b><font color="#019444">:</font> <font color="#052a57"><em>Would you mind waiting outside?</em></font><br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<b>would it be all right/​okay if...</b><font color="#019444">:</font> <font color="#052a57"><em>Would it be all right if I used your phone?</em></font><br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<font color="#019444"><font>Thesaurus:</font></font> <a href="entry://modal verbs">modal verbs</a><sub><font color="#af7f7f">hyponym</font></sub> <br>&nbsp;&nbsp;<font color="#b904af"><b>7.</b></font> <b><font color="#019444">used for offering something</font></b> <font color="#af7f7f">spoken</font> used when making a polite offer or invitation<br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<font color="#052a57"><em>Would you like a cup of coffee or something?</em></font><br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<font color="#052a57"><em>Would anyone care for a game of tennis?</em></font><br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<font color="#019444"><font>Thesaurus:</font></font> <a href="entry://modal verbs">modal verbs</a><sub><font color="#af7f7f">hyponym</font></sub> <br>&nbsp;&nbsp;<font color="#b904af"><b>8.</b></font> <b><font color="#019444">to be willing</font></b><br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<font color="#b904af"><b>8a.</b></font> used when you think someone is willing to do something<br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<font color="#052a57"><em>Bruce would lend you the money, I’m sure.</em></font><br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<font color="#019444"><font>Thesaurus:</font></font> <a href="entry://modal verbs">modal verbs</a><sub><font color="#af7f7f">hyponym</font></sub> <br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<font color="#b904af"><b>8b.</b></font> <font color="orangered">always in negatives</font> used for saying that someone refused to do something on a particular occasion<br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<font color="#052a57"><em>I asked her to help me, but she wouldn’t.</em></font><br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<font color="#019444"><font>Thesaurus:</font></font> <a href="entry://modal verbs">modal verbs</a><sub><font color="#af7f7f">hyponym</font></sub> <br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<font color="#af7f7f">hyponym</font></sub> <br>&nbsp;&nbsp;<font color="#b904af"><b>9.</b></font> <b><font color="#019444">used for saying what someone wants</font></b> used for politely saying what someone wants to do or wishes they could do<br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<b>would like/​love/​prefer etc to do something</b><font color="#019444">:</font> <font color="#052a57"><em>I think David would like to see you alone.</em></font><br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<font color="#052a57"><em>‘Come and spend Christmas with us.’ ‘I’d love to, but I you.</em></font><br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<font color="#052a57"><em>It would be wise to discuss this with your bank manager.</em></font><br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<font <b><font>her</font></b> <font color="#ff5400">strong</font> <font color="#ff5400">UK</font>  <font color="#21887d">[hɜː(r)]</font> <font color="#ff5400">US</font>  <font color="#21887d">[hɜr]</font> <font color="#ff5400">weak</font> <font color="#ff5400">UK</font>  <font color="#21887d">[ə(r)]</font> <font color="#ff5400">US</font>  <font color="#21887d">[ər]</font> <font color="#ff5400">UK</font>  <font color="#21887d">[hə(r)]</font> <font color="#ff5400">US</font>  <font color="#21887d">[hər]</font> <font color="#6020ae">determiner, pronoun</font> <font color="#ff5400">★★★</font><br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<font color="#019444"><i><font>Summary</font></i></font><br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; <b>Her</b> can be used in the following ways:<br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;as a pronoun , being the object form of <b>she</b> : <font color="#052a57"><em>If you see Mary, give her my love.</em></font><br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;in a one-word answer or after the verb ‘to be’: <font color="#052a57"><em>‘Who’s next?’ ‘Her.’</em></font> <font color="#019444">♦</font> <font color="#052a57"><em>Isn’t that her in the green coat?</em></font><br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;as a possessive determiner (followed by a noun), being a possessive form of <b>she</b> : <font color="#052a57"><em>She was holding her baby.</em></font><br>&nbsp;&nbsp;<font color="#b904af"><b>1.</b></font> used for referring to a woman, girl, or female animal when they have already been mentioned or when it is obvious which one you are referring to<br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<font color="#052a57"><em>Where’s Susan? Has anyone seen her?</em></font><br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<font color="#052a57"><em>‘Is that the boss’s wife?’ ‘Yes, I’m sure it’s her.’</em></font><br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<font color="#052a57"><em>She asked me to write to her.</em></font><br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<font color="#019444"><font>Thesaurus:</font></font> <a href="entry://personal pronouns">personal pronouns</a><sub><font color="#af7f7f">hyponym</font></sub> <br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<font color="#b904af"><b>1a.</b></font> belonging to her, or relating to her<br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<font color="#052a57"><em>She parked her car across the road.</em></font><br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<font color="#052a57"><em>Emma’s invited us to her party.</em></font><br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<font color="#052a57"><em>One of the employees lost her job.</em></font><br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<b>her own</b><font color="#019444">:</font> <font color="#052a57"><em>She makes her own clothes.</em></font><br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<font color="#019444"><font>Thesaurus:</font></font> <a href="entry://possessive pronouns">possessive pronouns</a><sub><font color="#af7f7f">hyponym</font></sub> <br>&nbsp;&nbsp;<font color="#b904af"><b>2.</b></font> <font color="#af7f7f">mainly literary</font> used for referring to a nation, a ship, or a car when it has already been mentioned or when it is obvious which one you are referring to<br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<font color="#052a57"><em>Britain and her allies</em></font><br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<font color="#019444"><font>Thesaurus:</font></font> <a href="entry://personal pronouns">personal pronouns</a><sub><font color="#af7f7f">hyponym</font></sub> <br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<font color="#019444"><font>See also:</font></font> <a href="entry://them">them</a>

all
<b><font>all</font></b> <font color="#ff5400">UK</font>  <font color="#21887d">[ɔːl]</font> <font color="#ff5400">US</font>  <font color="#21887d">[ɔl]</font> <font color="#6020ae">adverb, determiner, preposition, pronoun</font> <font color="#ff5400">★★★</font><br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<font color="#019444"><i><font>Summary</font></i></font><br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; <b>All</b> can be used in the following ways:<br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;as a determiner (followed by an uncountable or plural noun): <font color="#052a57"><em>They had given up all hope.</em></font> <font color="#019444">♦</font> <font color="#052a57"><em>All children deserve encouragement.</em></font><br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;as a predeterminer (followed by a word such as ‘the’, ‘this’, or ‘his’): <font color="#052a57"><em>I want to hear all the details.</em></font> <font color="#019444">♦</font> <font color="#052a57"><em>We lost all our money.</em></font><br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;as a pronoun : <font color="#052a57"><em>All was quiet in the street outside.</em></font> (before a relative clause): <font color="#052a57"><em>I’ve done all that I can to help her.</em></font> (followed by <b>of</b> ): <font color="#052a57"><em>I want to invite all of you.</em></font> (after the subject of a sentence): <font color="#052a57"><em>These buildings all belong to the college.</em></font> (following the pronoun object of a sentence): <font color="#052a57"><em>Pauline said goodbye to them all.</em></font> (after a modal or auxiliary verb or the verb ‘to be’): <font color="#052a57"><em>We can all relax.</em></font> <font color="#019444">♦</font> <font color="#052a57"><em>The tickets had all been sold.</em></font><br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;as an adverb (before an adjective, adverb, preposition, or conjunction): <font color="#052a57"><em>Bernard was all alone in a strange city.</em></font> <font color="#019444">♦</font> <font color="#052a57"><em>They forgot all about everything else.</em></font><br>&nbsp;&nbsp;<font color="#b904af"><b>1.</b></font> <b><font color="#019444">the whole of something</font></b><br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<font color="#b904af"><b>1a.</b></font> the whole of an amount or every part of something<br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<font color="#052a57"><em>There’s no cake left. <b><font>my</font></b> <font color="#ff5400">UK</font>  <font color="#21887d">[maɪ]</font> <font color="#ff5400">US</font>  <font color="#6020ae">determiner, interjection</font> <font color="#ff5400">★★★</font><br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<font color="#019444"><i><font>Summary</font></i></font><br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; <b>My</b> can be used in the following ways:<br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;as a possessive determiner (followed by a noun), being a possessive form of <b>I</b> : <font color="#052a57"><em>I’ve lost my sunglasses.</em></font><br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;as an interjection : <font color="#052a57"><em>My!
