about
<b><font>about</font></b> <font color="#ff5400">UK</font>  <font color="#21887d">[əˈbaʊt]</font> <font color="#ff5400">US</font>  <font color="#6020ae">adverb, preposition</font> <font color="#ff5400">★★★</font><br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<font color="#019444"><i><font>Summary</font></i></font><br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; <b>About</b> can be used in the following ways:<br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;as a preposition (followed by a noun): <font color="#052a57"><em>He told me about your problem.</em></font><br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;as an adverb (without a following noun): <font color="#052a57"><em>Stop rushing about.</em></font><br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;after the verb ‘to be’: <font color="#052a57"><em>Is your father about?</em></font><br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;followed by an infinitive with ‘to’: <font color="#052a57"><em>I was just about to explain.</em></font> <br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<font color="#019444"><i><font><br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Learner Errors </font></i></font>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;About or <a href="entry://around">around</a> ? In meanings 2, 3, 4, 5, 6, and 9, <a href="entry://around">around</a> is often used instead of <a href="entry://about">about</a> . Where a meaning of <a href="entry://about">about</a> is labelled British , <a href="entry://around">around</a> is the usual American word. <br>&nbsp;&nbsp;<font color="#b904af"><b>1.</b></font> <b><font color="#019444">concerning a particular subject</font></b><br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<font color="#b904af"><b>1a.</b></font> used for stating who or what you are discussing, considering, describing, forgetting etc<br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<font color="#052a57"><em>Think about what I’ve told you.</em></font><br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<font color="#052a57"><em>She kept saying horrible things about my mother.</em></font><br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<font color="#052a57"><em>jokes about the president</em></font><br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<b>all about</b><font color="#019444">:</font> <font color="#052a57"><em>They’d forgotten all about poor Harry.</em></font><br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<font color="#019444"><font>Thesaurus:</font></font> <a href="entry://concerning or about something">concerning or about something</a><sub><font color="#af7f7f">synonym</font></sub> <br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<font color="#b904af"><b>1b.</b></font> used for stating who or what your feelings and attitudes are directed towards<br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<font color="#052a57"><em>I’m worried about Dad.</em></font><br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<font color="#052a57"><em>There’s nothing to get excited about.</em></font><br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<font color="#019444"><font>Thesaurus:</font></font> <a href="entry://concerning or about something">concerning or about something</a><sub><font color="#af7f7f">synonym</font></sub> <br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<font color="#b904af"><b>1c.</b></font> <font color="#af7f7f">spoken</font> used for introducing a subject that you want to discuss<br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<font color="#052a57"><em>About that money I owe you – I can pay you back next week.</em></font><br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<font color="#052a57"><em>It’s about Jack – he’s been so depressed lately.</em></font><br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<font color="#019444"><font>Thesaurus:</font></font> <a href="entry://concerning or about something">concerning or about something</a><sub><font color="#af7f7f">synonym</font></sub> <br>&nbsp;&nbsp;<font color="#b904af"><b>2.</b></font> <b><font color="#019444">not exactly a particular amount or number</font></b><br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<font color="#b904af"><b>2a.</b></font> used for showing that you are guessing at an amount or number<br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<font color="#052a57"><em>About 250 people were killed in the explosion.</em></font><br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<font color="#052a57"><em>Anthea must be about the same age as you.</em></font><br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<font color="#019444"><font>Thesaurus:</font></font> <a href="entry://describing and introducing guesses">describing and introducing guesses</a><sub><font color="#af7f7f">hyponym</font></sub> <a href="entry://to guess">to guess</a><sub><font color="#af7f7f">synonym</font></sub> <br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<font color="#b904af"><b>2b.</b></font> used for referring to a time that is not exact<br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<font color="#052a57"><em>I woke up at about 3 am.</em></font><br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<b>round about</b><font color="#019444">:</font> <font color="#052a57"><em>It must have been round about six when we got home.</em></font><br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<font color="#019444"><font>Thesaurus:</font></font> <a href="entry://telling the time by a clock">telling the time by a clock</a><sub><font color="#af7f7f">hyponym</font></sub> <br>&nbsp;&nbsp;<font color="#b904af"><b>3.</b></font> <b><font color="#019444">used for showing movement</font></b><br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<font color="#b904af"><b>3a.</b></font> moving to many different parts or areas, or in different directions<br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<font color="#052a57"><em>The girls were dancing about the know
<b><font color="#b904af">▪ <font>I.</font></font> <font>know</font></b> <sup>1</sup> <font color="#ff5400">UK</font>  <font color="#21887d">[nəʊ]</font> <font color="#ff5400">US</font>  <font color="#21887d">[noʊ]</font> <font color="#6020ae">verb</font> <font color="orangered">never progressive</font> <font color="#af7f7f">[</font><font color="#af7f7f"><i>present tense</i></font> <font color="#af7f7f"><i>I/you/we/they</i></font> <font color="#019444">know</font> <font color="#af7f7f"><i>he/she/it</i></font> <font color="#019444">knows</font> <font color="#af7f7f"><i>present participle</i></font> <font color="#019444">knowing</font> <font color="#af7f7f"><i>past tense</i></font> <font color="#019444">knew</font> <font color="#21887d">[njuː]</font> <font color="#21887d">[nu]</font> <font color="#af7f7f"><i>past participle</i></font> <font color="#019444">known</font> <font color="#21887d">[nəʊn]</font> <font color="#21887d">[noʊn]</font><font color="#af7f7f">]</font> <font color="#ff5400">★★★</font> <br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<font color="#019444"><i><font><br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Ways of saying I don’t know </font></i></font>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Dunno<br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;used informally, in spoken language<br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;I have no idea / I haven’t a clue / I haven’t the faintest idea<br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;used when you have no information and you are unable to guess the answer to a question<br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;How should I know? / Don’t ask me / Search me<br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;used when you do not know something and you feel annoyed that someone is asking you about it<br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Who knows? / It’s anyone’s guess<br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;used for saying that you don’t know something because it is impossible for anyone to know it<br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Your guess is as good as mine<br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;used for saying that you know as little about something as the person who asked you about it<br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Not as far as I know<br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;used for saying that something may be true, but you do not have enough information to know whether it is or not<br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Examples:<br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<font color="#052a57"><em>‘Are you coming out later?’ ‘</em></font> Dunno. <font color="#052a57"><em>Depends on the weather.’</em></font><br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<font color="#052a57"><em>‘What time does the film start?’ ‘</em></font> I have no idea. <font color="#052a57"><em>Why don’t you call the cinema?’</em></font> <font color="#019444">♦</font> <font color="#052a57"><em>‘I don’t suppose you know where Braganza Street is?’ ‘</em></font> I haven’t a clue. <font color="#052a57"><em>Sorry.’</em></font> <font color="#019444">♦</font> <font color="#052a57"><em>‘Could somebody please explain how this car ended up in my driveway?’ ‘</em></font> I haven’t the faintest idea. <font color="#052a57"><em>’</em></font><br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<font color="#052a57"><em>‘Who left this rubbish all over the table?’ ‘</em></font> How should I know? <font color="#052a57"><em>I’ve only just come home.’</em></font> <font color="#019444">♦</font> <font color="#052a57"><em>‘Why didn’t he call me himself?’ ‘</em></font> Don’t ask me. <font color="#052a57"><em>I’m only the messenger.’</em></font> <font color="#019444">♦</font> <font color="#052a57"><em>‘Why didn’t he say he wasn’t coming?’ ‘</em></font> Search me. <font color="#052a57"><em>He never tells me anything.’</em></font><br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<font color="#052a57"><em>‘When will this situation ever be resolved?’ ‘</em></font> Who knows? will
<b><font color="#b904af">▪ <font>I.</font></font> <font>will</font></b> <sup>1</sup> <font color="#ff5400">UK</font>  <font color="#21887d">[wɪl]</font> <font color="#ff5400">US</font>  <font color="#6020ae">modal verb</font> <font color="#ff5400">★★★</font><br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<font color="#019444"><i><font>Summary</font></i></font><br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; <b>Will</b> is usually followed by an infinitive without ‘to’: <font color="#052a57"><em>She will be angry.</em></font> Sometimes it is used without a following infinitive: <font color="#052a57"><em>I never have borrowed money, and I never will.</em></font><br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;In conversation or informal writing <b>will</b> is often shortened to <b>’ll</b> : <font color="#052a57"><em>Do you think it’ll rain?</em></font><br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; <b>Will</b> does not change its form, so the third person singular form does not end in ‘-s’: <font color="#052a57"><em>Robert will be there.</em></font><br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Questions and negatives are formed without ‘do’: <font color="#052a57"><em>Will you help me?</em></font> <font color="#019444">♦</font> <font color="#052a57"><em>They will not accept our offer.</em></font><br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;The negative form <b>will not</b> is often shortened to <b>won’t</b> in conversation or informal writing: <font color="#052a57"><em>Don’t worry – the dog won’t bite you.</em></font><br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; <b>Will</b> is often used in question tags: <font color="#052a57"><em>You won’t tell Dad, will you?</em></font><br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; <b>Will</b> has no participles and no infinitive form. It is used for forming the future tense of other verbs, but does not have a future tense of its own.<br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; <b>Would</b> can sometimes be used as the past tense of <b>will</b> , for example in indirect speech introduced by a verb in the past tense: <font color="#052a57"><em>He promised that he would return.</em></font><br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; <b>Will have</b> forms the future perfect tense, which is used for describing actions that are expected to be completed before a time in the future: <font color="#052a57"><em>By the end of the course, you will have learned all the basic skills.</em></font><br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<font color="#b904af"><b>1.</b></font> <b><font color="#019444">used for talking about future actions or events</font></b><br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<font color="#b904af"><b>1a.</b></font> used for saying what you expect to happen in the future<br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<font color="#052a57"><em>Let’s finish the job now – it won’t take long.</em></font><br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<font color="#052a57"><em>Who do you think will win on as
<b><font>as</font></b> <font color="#ff5400">strong</font> <font color="#ff5400">UK</font>  <font color="#21887d">[æz]</font> <font color="#ff5400">US</font>  <font color="#ff5400">weak</font> <font color="#ff5400">★★★</font><br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<font color="#019444"><i><font>Summary</font></i></font><br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; <b>As</b> can be used in the following ways:<br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;as a conjunction (connecting two clauses): <font color="#052a57"><em>As I was leaving, the phone rang.</em></font> <font color="#019444">♦</font> <font color="#052a57"><em>The results were not as bad as I had expected.</em></font><br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;as a preposition (followed by a noun): <font color="#052a57"><em>He works as a waiter.</em></font><br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;as an adverb (followed by an adjective, an adverb, or a word such as ‘much’ or ‘many’): <font color="#052a57"><em>Nylon is cheaper than leather, and it’s just as strong.</em></font><br>&nbsp;&nbsp;<font color="#b904af"><b>1.</b></font> <b><font color="#019444">used for showing comparison</font></b><br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<font color="#b904af"><b>1a.</b></font> used for comparing one person, thing, or situation with another<br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<b>as...as</b><font color="#019444">:</font> <font color="#052a57"><em>Simon isn’t as tall as his brother.</em></font><br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<font color="#052a57"><em>I don’t play football as much as I used to.</em></font><br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<font color="#052a57"><em>I can’t run as fast as you.</em></font><br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<b>just as</b><font color="#019444">:</font> <font color="#052a57"><em>We all need regular exercise, but a healthy diet is just as important.</em></font><br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<b>half/​twice/​three times etc as much</b><font color="#019444">:</font> <font color="#052a57"><em>A house in London costs twice as much as a similar house in Liverpool.</em></font><br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<b>the same as</b><font color="#019444">:</font> <font color="#052a57"><em>Barbara’s suggestion was almost exactly the same as mine.</em></font><br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<font color="#b904af"><b>1b.</b></font> used in particular expressions for emphasizing a quality in someone or something<br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<font color="#052a57"><em>Her skin was white as snow.</em></font><br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<font color="#052a57"><em>as tough as old boots</em></font><br>&nbsp;&nbsp;<font color="#b904af"><b>2.</b></font> <b><font
